[5:0:191,267] 0750   Office of the Lieutenant Governor  

[6:0:66,288] Under California's Constitution, the Lieutenant Governor serves as Acting Governor whenever the Governor is absent from the  

[6:1:66,298] state, and automatically becomes Governor if a vacancy occurs in the Office of Governor. The Lieutenant Governor is also  

[6:2:66,308] President of the Senate and votes in case of a tie.  

[7:0:66,326] The Lieutenant Governor serves as a voting member of the Board of Regents of the University of California, the Board of  

[7:1:66,336] Trustees of the California State University system, and the Board of Governors of the California Community Colleges system.  

[7:2:66,347] The Lieutenant Governor also sits on the Calbright College Board of Trustees.  

[7:3:66,364] The Lieutenant Governor also serves on, and rotates with the State Controller, as chair of the three-member State Lands  

[7:4:66,374] Commission, which oversees the control and leasing of millions of acres of state-owned land, including offshore oil resources,  

[7:5:66,385] as well as use and permitting for all navigable waterways in California. The Commission also manages state land-use planning  

[7:6:66,395] and revenues, and related interstate issues. During alternate years, when the Lieutenant Governor serves as Chairperson of  

[7:7:66,405] the State Lands Commission, the Lieutenant Governor also serves as a member of the Ocean Protection Council   and as a  

[7:8:66,415] non-voting member of the California Coastal Commission.  

[8:0:66,433] In addition, under state statutes, the Lieutenant Governor chairs the California Commission for Economic Development, which  

[8:1:66,443] provides support and guidance to the Governor, Legislature, and private sector regarding the development of California's  

[8:2:66,453] economy.

[8:0:224,380] 0820   Department of Justice  

[9:0:66,402] The constitutional office of the Attorney General, as chief law officer of the state, has the responsibility to see that the laws of  

[9:1:66,412] California are uniformly and adequately enforced. This responsibility is fulfilled through the diverse programs of the Department  

[9:2:66,422] of Justice.  

[10:0:66,442] The Department of Justice is responsible for providing skillful and efficient legal services on behalf of the people of California.  

[10:1:66,453] The Attorney General represents the people in all matters before the Appellate and Supreme Courts of California and the  

[10:2:66,463] United States; serves as legal counsel to state officers, boards, commissioners, and departments; represents the people in  

[10:3:66,473] actions to protect the environment and to enforce consumer, antitrust, and civil laws; and assists district attorneys in the  

[10:4:66,483] administration of justice. The Department provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms/ 

[10:5:66,493] dangerous weapon laws; provides evaluation and analysis of physical evidence; regulates legal gambling activities in  

[10:6:66,504] California; supports the telecommunications and data processing needs of the California criminal justice community; and  

[10:7:66,514] pursues projects designed to protect the people of California from fraudulent, unfair, and illegal activities.

[7:0:66,189] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[8:0:65,209] • DNA ID Fund Restoration—The Budget includes $35.4 million one-time General Fund to backfill a decline in fine and fee  

[8:1:76,219] revenues to maintain current service levels to process forensic evidence for local jurisdictions.  

[9:0:65,235] • Fentanyl Enforcement Program—The Budget includes $7.8 million General Fund in 2022-23, and $6.7 million in 2023-24  

[9:1:76,245] and ongoing to augment DOJ’s law enforcement task forces to include a Fentanyl Enforcement Program to target fentanyl-

[9:2:76,256] trafficking criminal networks across the state.  

[10:0:65,272] • Organized Retail Theft Prevention—The Budget includes $6 million General Fund annually in 2022-23 through 2024-25,  

[10:1:76,282] $361,000 in 2025-26, and $500,000 ongoing to combat organized retail theft and prosecute retail theft cases that span  

[10:2:76,292] multiple jurisdictions. Resources will support investigations, prosecutions, and data analytics for coordinated efforts against  

[10:3:76,302] retail theft.  

[11:0:65,319] • Local Law Enforcement Task Force Coordination—The Budget includes $5 million ongoing General Fund to support DOJ  

[11:1:76,329] participation in tasks forces across the state that aid local law enforcement agencies in crime suppression efforts.  

[12:0:65,345] • Sex Offender Registration—The Budget includes $4.5 million General Fund in 2022-23, and $2.2 million ongoing, to address  

[12:1:76,355] both the immediate and long-term workload associated with re-tiering and terminating offenders on the sex offender registry  

[12:2:76,365] pursuant to Chapter 541, Statutes of 2018 (SB 384).  

[13:0:65,382] • Police Use of Force—The Budget includes $2.3 million General Fund in 2022-23, and $1.6 million ongoing to support DOJ’s  

[13:1:76,392] ability to physically appear and respond to an event to determine whether it requires a full investigation pursuant to Chapter  

[13:2:76,402] 326, Statutes of 2020 (AB 1506).  

[14:0:65,418] • Peace Officers: Release of Records (SB 16)—The Budget includes $7.4 million ($3.4 million General Fund and $4 million  

[14:1:76,428] Legal Services Revolving Fund) to prepare records pertaining to police officer conduct for public disclosure pursuant to  

[14:2:76,439] Chapter 402, Statutes of 2021 (SB 16).  

[15:0:65,455] • Law Enforcement Gangs (AB 958)—The Budget includes $1.3 million General Fund in 2022-23 and $1.2 million ongoing to  

[15:1:76,465] respond to additional investigations that fall within the expanded definition of “law enforcement gangs” pursuant to Chapter  

[15:2:76,475] 408, Statutes of 2021 (AB   958).  

[16:0:65,491] • Firearms Information Technology System Modernization Project—The Budget includes $5.2 million one-time Dealer Record  

[16:1:76,502] of Sale Special Account to continue support for project planning activities to consolidate existing firearms information  

[16:2:76,512] technology systems. To date, the state has invested $2.4 million for this Project.  

[17:0:65,528] • Firearms Precursor Parts (AB 879)—The Budget includes $223,000 ongoing General Fund to address the accelerated  

[17:1:76,538] timeline and resource needs related to regulating the sale and transfer of firearm precursor parts pursuant to Chapter 730,  

[17:2:76,548] Statutes of 2020 (AB 879).  

[18:0:65,565] • Firearms Tracing (AB 1191)—The Budget includes $327,000 General Fund in 2022-23 and $306,000 ongoing to analyze  

[18:1:76,575] and report on firearms that were illegally possessed, used in a crime, or suspected to have been used in a crime.  

[19:0:65,591] • Firearms Transfers (SB 715)—The Budget includes $2.3 million ($6,000 General Fund and $2.3 million Dealer Record of  

[19:1:76,601] Sale Special Account) in 2022-23, decreasing to $973,000 ($3,000 General Fund and $970,000 Dealers Record of Sale  

[19:2:76,611] Special Account) in 2026-27 and ongoing, to facilitate and maintain multiple modifications to firearms databases to align with  

[19:3:76,622] firearm transfer laws.  

[20:0:65,638] • Medi-Cal Fraud and Elder Abuse: Medicaid Patient Abuse Prevention Act—The Budget includes $7.8 million ($6.1 million  

[20:1:76,648] Federal Trust Fund, $1.2 million False Claims Act Fund, and $474,000 General Fund) in 2022-23 and $7.1 million ($5.6  

[20:2:76,658] million Federal Trust Fund, $1.1 million False Claims Act Fund, and $406,000 General Fund) in 2023-24 and ongoing to  

[20:3:76,668] provide sufficient authority for DOJ to receive the full amount of a reoccurring federal grant that supports investigative,  

[20:4:76,679] enforcement, and prosecutorial duties carried out by the Department’s Division of Medi-Cal Fraud and Elder Abuse.  

[21:0:65,695] • Reproductive Health Care Services (AB 1356)—The Budget includes $879,000 General Fund in 2022-23 and $671,000  

[21:1:76,705] ongoing to implement new data reporting requirements, prepare an annual report that details anti-reproductive healthcare

[5:0:66,406] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,425] 0435 - LEGAL SERVICES  

[7:0:66,445] Legal Services is organized into four elements: (1) Civil Law, (2) Criminal Law,   (3) Public Rights, and (4) Medi-Cal and Elder  

[7:1:66,456] Abuse.  

[8:0:66,476] Civil Law represents the State of California and its officers, agencies, departments, boards, commissions, and employees in  

[8:1:66,486] civil matters. It provides advice to these clients, defends cases brought against them, prosecutes cases to vindicate state  

[8:2:66,496] interests, and conducts investigations. Deputy Attorneys General in Civil Law are responsible for managing and litigating cases  

[8:3:66,507] before administrative tribunals, and in both state and federal courts at the trial level and on appeal, including appeals before the  

[8:4:66,517] United States and California Supreme Courts. Deputies work in one of   nine sections: Business Litigation; Cannabis Control;  

[8:5:66,527] Correctional Law; Employment and Administrative Mandate; Government Law; Health, Education, and Welfare; Health Quality  

[8:6:66,537] Enforcement; Licensing; and Tort and Condemnation.  

[9:0:66,558] Criminal Law represents the   People of the State of California   in criminal matters before the Appellate and Supreme courts.  

[9:1:66,568] Criminal Law also fulfills the Attorney General's responsibilities of assisting district attorneys in cases for which they are  

[9:2:66,578] recused, conducting criminal investigations, representing the Governor, Board of Parole Hearings, and California Department of  

[9:3:66,588] Corrections and Rehabilitation in state and federal habeas corpus cases and appeals, and other proceedings relating to parole  

[9:4:66,598] decisions and conditions of confinement in the state prisons, and defending criminal judgements in state and federal habeas  

[9:5:66,609] corpus matters. Additional responsibilities include enforcing the Political Reform Act, advising the Governor on extradition  

[9:6:66,619] matters, and investigating, prosecuting, and coordinating litigation involving white-collar crimes, high-tech/computer/privacy  

[9:7:66,629] crimes, financial crimes, human trafficking, environmental crimes, public corruption, and officer-involved shootings.  

[10:0:66,649] Public Rights protects and preserves the public’s interests by providing legal services to state agencies, boards and  

[10:1:66,660] commissions, and Constitutional Officers, and by bringing actions in the name of the Attorney General to protect the public.  

[10:2:66,670] Public Rights provides specialized services in the following areas: Civil Rights Enforcement (including the Bureau of Children's  

[10:3:66,680] Justice); Racial Justice; Disability Rights; Worker Rights and Fair Labor; Charitable Trusts Enforcement and Regulation  

[10:4:66,690] (including the Registry of Charitable Trusts); Natural Resources Law; Corporate Fraud (including False Claims, Energy and  

[10:5:66,700] Corporate Responsibility); Healthcare Rights and Access (including Tobacco Litigation and Enforcement, and Healthcare  

[10:6:66,711] Competition and Pharmaceutical pricing); Indian and Gaming Law; Environment Law (including the Bureau of Environmental  

[11:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 152 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — LJE   150 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:189,32] 0820   Department of Justice - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] Justice); Land Use and Conservation; Consumer Protection (including Privacy Enforcement and Sellers of Travel); and Antitrust  

[3:1:66,79] Law.  

[4:0:66,97] The Division of Medi-Cal Fraud and Elder Abuse represents the People of the State of California in both criminal and civil  

[4:1:66,107] matters involving Medi-Cal provider fraud, the abuse or neglect of elder and dependent adults in residential facilities, and the  

[4:2:66,117] abuse and neglect of Medi-Cal recipients in non-institutional settings. The Division is a vertical prosecution unit whose  

[4:3:66,127] investigations are conducted by multidisciplinary teams consisting of Special Agents, Investigative Auditors, Digital Forensic  

[4:4:66,137] Specialists, Registered Nurses, and Deputy Attorneys General. Deputy Attorneys General from the Division represent the  

[4:5:66,148] People of the State of California in both federal and state courts. Types of cases frequently prosecuted by the Division include  

[4:6:66,158] fraud committed against the Medi-Cal program by doctors, pharmacies, clinics, dentists, medical equipment suppliers, hospice,  

[4:7:66,168] home health companies, and all other Medi-Cal providers; elder or dependent adult abuse or neglect in skilled nursing facilities,  

[4:8:66,178] residential care facilities for the elderly, intermediate care facilities for the developmentally disabled, and other specified  

[4:9:66,188] residential care facilities; and the neglect or abuse of Medi-Cal recipients in non-institutional settings, when such abuse or  

[4:10:66,199] neglect is connected to the provision of case.  

[5:0:66,216] 0440 - LAW ENFORCEMENT  

[6:0:66,237] The Division of Law Enforcement is organized into five areas: (1) Bureau of Firearms, (2) Bureau of Forensic Services, (3)  

[6:1:66,247] Bureau of Gambling Control, (4) Bureau of Investigation, and (5) the Office of the Chief.  

[7:0:66,267] The Bureau of Firearms (BOF) provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms and  

[7:1:66,277] ammunition   laws by administering a multitude of different state-mandated firearms and ammunition-related programs. It is  

[7:2:66,288] accomplished by conducting firearm and ammunition eligibility checks, conducting compliance inspections at firearm dealers,  

[7:3:66,298] ammunition vendors, and manufacturers, and by providing valuable training to stakeholders statewide. BOF Special Agents  

[7:4:66,308] conduct investigations on armed and prohibited persons and other investigations resulting in the seizure of firearms,  

[7:5:66,318] magazines, and ammunition. Finally, BOF Special Agents conduct investigations to monitor and   prevent illegal   firearm  

[7:6:66,328] trafficking at permitted gun shows in accordance with state and federal laws.  

[8:0:66,349] The Bureau of Forensic Services (BFS) provides evaluation and scientific analysis of physical evidence, crime scene  

[8:1:66,359] investigation, and scientific investigative support for officer-involved shooting investigations. Additionally BFS provides expert  

[8:2:66,369] court testimony to federal, state and local law enforcement agencies, district attorneys, and courts. The BFS operates 10  

[8:3:66,379] regional crime laboratories and two specialized laboratories, the Jan Bashinski DNA Laboratory and Statewide Toxicology  

[8:4:66,390] Laboratory, which   serve 46 of California’s 58 counties. The BFS also operates the California Criminalistics Institute forensic  

[8:5:66,400] training facility that provides training for forensic scientists worldwide. Finally, BFS maintains the state DNA database, which  

[8:6:66,410] stores and regularly searches the DNA profiles of sex and violent offenders and felony arrestees against the DNA profiles of  

[8:7:66,420] evidence from unsolved crimes.  

[9:0:66,441] The Bureau of Gambling Control (BGC) regulates legal gambling activities in California to ensure gambling is conducted  

[9:1:66,451] honestly and is free from criminal and corruptive elements. This is accomplished by investigating the qualifications of  

[9:2:66,461] individuals and business entities who apply for licenses and monitoring the conduct of these licensees to ensure compliance  

[9:3:66,471] with the Gambling Control Act and applicable regulations. BGC conducts criminal investigations in and around tribal casinos  

[9:4:66,481] and California cardrooms. In addition, BGC conducts audits and reviews for tribal gaming to ensure that each tribe is in  

[9:5:66,492] compliance with all aspects of the state gaming compact.  

[10:0:66,512] The Bureau of Investigation (BI) is the premiere investigative bureau that is responsible for investigating and dismantling  

[10:1:66,522] criminal organizations, as well as assisting with the prosecution of serious criminal offenses that present a significant and multi-

[10:2:66,532] jurisdictional threat to California. The BI prioritizes investigations related to transnational criminal enterprises involved in gangs,  

[10:3:66,543] as well as cases involving major white-collar fraud, underground economy, recycle fraud, officer-involved shootings, homicides,  

[10:4:66,553] foreign prosecution, human trafficking and sexual predator apprehension crimes. In addition, BI serves a principal role in  

[10:5:66,563] providing leadership, coordination, and support to law enforcement through intelligence support centers and multi-agency task  

[10:6:66,573] forces focusing on violent offenders, gangs, and major crimes statewide.  

[11:0:66,594] The Office of the Chief (Office) provides administrative support to the investigative, regulatory, and forensic components of the  

[11:1:66,604] Division of Law Enforcement and other criminal justice agencies. The Office serves as the policy-making and oversight body for  

[11:2:66,614] its four operational bureaus.  

[12:0:66,632] 0445 - CALIFORNIA JUSTICE INFORMATION SERVICES  

[13:0:66,652] The California Justice Information Services Division provides criminal justice intelligence, information, and identification  

[13:1:66,662] services to law enforcement, regulatory agencies, and the public. Four major functional areas carry out these primary services:  

[13:2:66,673] 1) The Justice Data and Investigative Services Bureau consolidates the identification, investigative, and field services functions,  

[13:3:66,683] providing information and technical assistance on manual and automated systems including the fingerprint identification system  

[13:4:66,693] and the violent crime information system; 2) The Bureau of Criminal Information and Analysis consolidates the functions related  

[13:5:66,703] to the authorization, release, and use of criminal offender record information for law enforcement investigatory and regulatory  

[13:6:66,713] purposes; 3) The Hawkins Data Center operates the Criminal Justice Information System and the California Law Enforcement  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[10:0:242,447] 0840   State Controller  

[11:0:66,469] The State Controller is the chief fiscal officer of California. Principally responsible for transparency and accountability of the  

[11:1:66,479] state's financial resources, the Controller ensures the appropriate disbursement and tracking of taxpayer dollars. The Controller  

[11:2:66,489] serves on dozens of state boards, commissions, and committees with duties   ranging from   administrative oversight of the  

[11:3:66,499] nation's two largest public pension funds,   to protection of state lands and coastlines,   to modernization and financing of major  

[11:4:66,509] infrastructure. The Controller also offers fiscal guidance to local governments and has independent auditing authority over  

[11:5:66,520] government agencies related to the spending of state funds. The Controller's primary objectives are to:  

[11:6:65,537] • Account for and control disbursement of all state funds, issuing warrants in payment of the state's bills, including lottery  

[11:7:76,547] prizes.  

[11:8:65,564] • Determine legality and accuracy of financial claims against the state.  

[11:9:65,580] • Audit state and local government programs and agencies.  

[12:0:65,596] • Ensure businesses report and remit unclaimed property in compliance with Unclaimed Property Law and safeguard remitted  

[12:1:76,606] unclaimed property until claimed by the rightful owners or heirs.  

[12:2:65,622] • Inform the public of the state's financial condition.  

[12:3:65,639] • Inform the public of financial transactions of city, county, and other local governments.  

[12:4:65,655] • Administer the Uniform State Payroll System.  

[13:0:65,671] • Audit and process all personnel and payroll transactions for state civil service, state exempt employees, California State  

[13:1:76,681] University employees, and Judicial Council employees.  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:0:66,495] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,514] 0500100 - ACCOUNTING AND REPORTING  

[6:0:66,535] The State Accounting and Reporting Division maintains uniform and systematic control accounts of all receipts, payments,  

[6:1:66,545] appropriations, state fund balances, and bonded indebtedness; monitors the cash flow of the General Fund; administers the  

[6:2:66,555] statewide discharge from accountability program; participates in offsetting monies owed to the state; reports the financial  

[6:3:66,565] condition of the state; and collaborates with the Department of Finance, the Treasurer, and the Department of General Services  

[6:4:66,576] to develop and implement the Financial Information System for California (FI$Cal) to ensure the system meets the state's  

[6:5:66,586] primary objectives and provides best business practices for the state.  

[7:0:66,606] The Local Government Programs and Services Division maintains a database of information and reports on local financial  

[7:1:66,616] transactions and government compensation; apportions shared revenues to local governments; administers local mandated  

[7:2:66,627] and non-mandated cost reimbursement programs; approves county cost allocation plans; prescribes uniform accounting  

[7:3:66,637] procedures for counties, special districts, and trial court revenues; administers and collects estate and inheritance taxes;  

[7:4:66,647] collects delinquent insurance and motor vehicle fuel taxes, petroleum and gas assessments, and trial court penalties; refunds  

[7:5:66,657] gasoline taxes paid on fuel consumed for off-highway purposes; instructs and advises county tax collectors; approves state and  

[7:6:66,667] local government requests to participate in the Interagency Intercept Collection Program; and administers the Property Tax  

[7:7:66,678] Postponement Program for seniors and people with disabilities.  

[7:8:66,695] 0500200 - AUDITS  

[8:0:66,716] The Audits Division determines the legality and accuracy of all claims against the state through the performance of prepayment  

[9:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] audits; assures the accuracy of local government claims and financial statements submitted to the state and federal

[4:3:66,109] Property Law.  

[5:0:66,127] 0500300 - PERSONNEL AND PAYROLL SERVICES  

[6:0:66,148] The Personnel and Payroll Services Division administers the state's payroll, employment history, automated travel expense  

[6:1:66,158] reimbursement system, and leave accounting processes. The Division works with the Department of Human Resources,  

[6:2:66,168] California Public Employees' Retirement System, California State Teachers' Retirement System, Judicial Council, Department  

[6:3:66,178] of Finance, and California State University Chancellor's Office to maximize the efficiency of the state's personnel and payroll  

[6:4:66,188] functions.  

[7:0:66,209] The California State Payroll System Project was initiated to modernize the statewide human resource management and  

[7:1:66,219] payroll   systems as part of a fully integrated solution. The system should enable the state to improve management processes  

[7:2:66,229] and fulfill its payroll, reporting, and deduction processing obligations accurately and on time.  

[7:3:66,247] 0500400 - UNCLAIMED PROPERTY  

[8:0:66,267] The Unclaimed Property Division administers the Unclaimed Property Law by providing one central source for owners to claim  

[8:1:66,277] their property; notifying owners of their unclaimed property before it is transferred to the state; receiving unclaimed property  

[8:2:66,288] from banks, savings and loans, insurance companies, and other businesses; and providing outreach and education for  

[8:3:66,298] businesses holding unclaimed property. 

[8:4:66,316] 0500500 - DISBURSEMENTS  

[9:0:66,336] The Disbursements Bureau produces and delivers all payments of the state's obligations after auditing and clearance through  

[9:1:66,346] control accounts.   Examples of some of the state's payments are personal income tax refunds, payroll, vendor payments,   and  

[9:2:66,356] retirement payments. Disbursements also provides post-issuance services including disposition of undeliverable warrants; lost  

[9:3:66,367] warrant duplication; and maintenance and production of paid warrant images.  

[9:4:66,384] 0500900 - DEPARTMENTAL ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,405] The Executive Office and the Administration Program provide executive direction and support services to all   divisions in the  

[10:1:66,415] State Controller's Office. The Information Systems Division (ISD)   develops, maintains, and operates all of the department's  

[10:2:66,425] mainframe, client-server, and web-based systems; and oversees the planning, procurement, use, and maintenance of  

[10:3:66,435] information technology hardware and software. Within ISD, the Information Security Office evaluates security compliance,  

[10:4:66,445] internal control management, and security governance.

[7:0:216,415] 0845   Department of Insurance  

[8:0:66,437] California's publicly-elected Insurance Commissioner regulates the third largest insurance economy in the world with insurance  

[8:1:66,447] companies collecting more than $371 billion in premiums annually in California while protecting consumers and ensuring the  

[8:2:66,457] health and sustainability of the insurance marketplace. The vision of the California Department of Insurance (CDI) is "Insurance  

[8:3:66,467] Protection for All Californians." CDI accomplishes this by enforcing insurance laws and regulations, assisting consumers in their  

[8:4:66,478] dealings with insurance companies, and enhancing business processes to better address emerging and future challenges as  

[8:5:66,488] well as improving services for insurance producers, consumers, and businesses.  

[9:0:66,505] CDI licenses and regulates insurance companies, and individuals in California. Currently, CDI oversees and licenses more than  

[9:1:66,516] 1,400 insurance companies and more than 450,000 individuals and business entities as insurance agents, brokers, adjusters,  

[9:2:66,526] and bail agents and annually issues approximately 225,000 licenses (new and renewals). Additionally, CDI receives and  

[9:3:66,536] investigates more than 210,000 consumer inquiries and complaints annually, performs hundreds of ongoing risk-focused  

[9:4:66,546] financial surveillances of insurance companies, receives more than 23,000 suspected fraudulent claim referrals and  

[10:0:66,556] investigates approximately 1,800 of those referrals, receives and reviews approximately 6,800 rate filing applications annually,  

[10:1:66,567] and works in conjunction with local, state, and federal law enforcement agencies to investigate and prosecute fraudulent  

[10:2:66,577] insurance practices.

[14:0:66,695] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[14:1:66,714] 0520 - REGULATION OF INSURANCE COMPANIES AND INSURANCE PRODUCERS  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — LJE   187 

[2:0:181,32] 0845   Department of Insurance - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The objectives of this program are to: (1) oversee the financial solvency of insurance companies to make sure they can provide  

[3:1:66,79] the benefits and protections promised to California policyholders; (2) review complex, principles-based reserving methods and  

[3:2:66,89] underlying assumptions to ensure transparency and consistency in models; (3) prevent unlawful or unfair practices by  

[3:3:66,99] insurance companies and insurance producers as defined by the Insurance Code; (4) ensure that property and casualty  

[3:4:66,109] insurance rates are not excessive, inadequate, unfairly discriminatory, or otherwise in violation of the California Insurance Code  

[3:5:66,120] and the California Code of Regulations; (5) assess and implement strategies to reduce climate risk impacts in the insurance  

[3:6:66,130] sector; (6) review health insurance rates filed with CDI to determine whether they are reasonable and work with insurance  

[3:7:66,140] companies to get unreasonable rates lowered; (7) review long term care insurance rates to ensure requested rate increases  

[3:8:66,150] are actuarially justified and not excessive; (8) ensure that applicants for insurance licenses, and holders of insurance licenses,  

[3:9:66,160] satisfy and maintain the qualifications for licensure. Additionally, CDI administers the estates of insolvent and delinquent  

[3:10:66,171] insurance companies through the Conservation and Liquidation Office.  

[3:11:66,188] 0525 - CONSUMER PROTECTION  

[4:0:66,206] The objectives of this program are to: (1) provide direct service to California consumers by protecting insurance policyholders  

[4:1:66,216] and other parties involved in insurance transactions against unfair or illegal practices with respect to claims handling, rating, or  

[4:2:66,226] underwriting by insurers and producers; (2) protect applicants and policyholders from discriminatory, unlawful, or fraudulent  

[4:3:66,237] practices and from incompetence relating to the sale of insurance; (3) oversee programs that benefit California's underserved  

[4:4:66,247] and historically disadvantaged communities; and (4) assist wildfire survivors, local governments, small businesses, community  

[4:5:66,257] service organizations, and neighborhood associations by providing access to CDI’s services through electronic and printed  

[4:6:66,267] informational guides, workshops, seminars, roundtables, and town halls.  

[4:7:66,285] 0530 - FRAUD CONTROL  

[5:0:66,303] The objective of this program is to protect the public from economic loss by actively investigating, arresting and referring for  

[5:1:66,313] prosecution those who commit insurance fraud and other violations of the law. The program is primarily staffed by sworn peace  

[5:2:66,323] officers who conduct criminal investigations of insurance fraud and related criminal cases. The program administers the  

[5:3:66,333] Insurance Frauds Prevention Act (IFPA), which authorizes CDI to conduct criminal insurance fraud investigations. In addition,  

[5:4:66,343] the IFPA authorizes the Commissioner to initiate or intervene in whistle-blower "qui tam" actions seeking civil penalties against  

[5:5:66,354] perpetrators of insurance fraud.  

[6:0:66,371] 0535 - GENERAL FUND TAX COLLECTION AND COMPLIANCE  

[7:0:66,389] This program performs tax collection, ensures the compliance of insurance companies and surplus line brokers with the laws  

[7:1:66,399] contained in the Insurance Code and the Revenue and Taxation Code, and works with the California Department of Tax and  

[7:2:66,409] Fee Administration and the State Controller's Office on various refund, assessment, and accounting matters relative to the  

[7:3:66,420] premium tax program. Tax collections from this program are deposited in the state's General Fund.  

[8:0:66,460] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[10:0:183,619] 0850   California State Lottery Commission  

[11:0:66,641] In 1984, Proposition 37 amended the California Constitution to authorize the establishment of a statewide lottery. As an  

[12:0:66,651] initiative statute, the California State Lottery Act (Act) of 1984 created the California State Lottery Commission and gave it  

[13:0:66,661] broad powers to oversee the operations of a statewide lottery. The purpose of the Act was to provide supplemental monies to  

[13:1:66,671] benefit public education. The Lottery is overseen by a five-person Commission appointed by the Governor and confirmed by  

[13:2:66,681] the State Senate.  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 195 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — LJE   193 

[2:0:148,32] 0850   California State Lottery Commission - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Act initially required that 50 percent of total annual revenues be returned to the public in the form of prizes and at least 34  

[3:1:66,79] percent of total revenues be allocated to the benefit of public education. No more than 16 percent of total revenues were to be  

[3:2:66,89] used for administrative costs.  

[4:0:66,107] In 2010, the Act was changed to allow the Lottery flexibility to pay out more money in prizes and reduce the administrative cost  

[4:1:66,117] limit to 13 percent of total revenues. Along with that flexibility, the new law requires the Lottery to meet minimum levels of  

[4:2:66,127] contribution to public education. Revenues to education are placed in a special fund, known as the California State Lottery  

[4:3:66,137] Education Fund, which holds revenues until they are allocated on a per capita basis, using prior year certified Average Daily  

[4:4:66,148] Attendance data, to the following categories: K-12 education, Community Colleges, the California State University, the  

[4:5:66,158] University of California, and other educational entities, including the California Schools for the Deaf and Blind.  

[4:6:66,175] In the 36 years since sales began in October 1985 through June 30, 2021, the California State Lottery has raised $39.4 billion  

[4:7:66,186] for public education, including approximately $1.9 billion in FY 2020-21.  

[5:0:66,203] Because of the inherently variable nature of lottery ticket sales, revenue estimates for 2021-22 and 2022-23 cannot be made  

[5:1:66,214] with certainty.

[6:1:66,260] DEPARTMENT AUTHORITY  

[6:2:66,280] Government Code, Title 2, Division 1, Chapter 12.5 (Sections 8880-8880.72).

[0:0:66,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — LJE   196   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:169,66] 0855   California Gambling Control Commission  

[2:0:66,87] The mission of the California Gambling Control Commission (Commission) is to protect the public by ensuring integrity and  

[2:1:66,97] justice in California's controlled gambling industry through effective regulations and fair application of the law. The Commission  

[2:2:66,108] has jurisdiction over gambling establishments (cardrooms), third-party providers of proposition player services, and certain  

[2:3:66,118] aspects of Tribal casinos, pursuant to its authority under state law and Tribal-State Gaming Compacts (Compacts). The  

[2:4:66,128] Commission also has jurisdiction over gaming policies, regulations, criteria, and standards.  

[3:0:66,146] There are 86 licensed cardrooms in California over which the Commission has broad regulatory and adjudicatory authority. This  

[3:1:66,156] authority extends to the operation, concentration, and supervision of the cardrooms and all persons and things related to each  

[3:2:66,166] licensed establishment.  

[4:0:66,184] The Commission has fiduciary, regulatory, and administrative responsibilities related to Tribal gaming that include: (1)  

[4:1:66,194] distributing specified Tribal gaming revenues to Non-Compact, Non-Gaming and Limited-Gaming Tribes; (2) making suitability  

[4:2:66,204] determinations for key employees, gaming resource suppliers, and financial sources; and (3) serving as the administrator of the  

[4:3:66,214] Indian Gaming Revenue Sharing Trust Fund, Indian Gaming Special Distribution Fund, and the Tribal Nation Grant Fund.

[5:0:209,169] 0860   State Board of Equalization  

[5:1:66,191] The State Board of Equalization's (BOE)   duties   primarily include assessing and allocating the property values of railroads and  

[5:2:66,201] specified utilities and businesses; adjudicating property tax appeals of taxable government owned property; overseeing the  

[5:3:66,211] property tax assessment practices of the 58 county assessors; adopting rules to clarify property tax laws; and administering the  

[5:4:66,221] alcoholic beverage excise tax and the insurance tax, including appeals. The BOE contracts with the   California Department of  

[5:5:66,232] Tax and Fee Administration (CDTFA)   to administer the alcoholic beverage tax and insurance tax program.

[5:0:66,457] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,477] 0570025 - COUNTY ASSESSMENT STANDARDS PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,494] This program ensures that taxable properties are enrolled and assessed by the 58 county assessors in full conformity with the  

[6:1:66,505] law. The BOE is also charged with providing consultation and services to the county assessors and their staff, establishing  

[6:2:66,515] standards, providing training for assessors and assessment appeals boards, evaluating the effectiveness of each county  

[6:3:66,525] assessor's administration, co-administering the welfare exemption, and administering the Legal Entity Ownership Program.  

[6:4:66,543] 0570050 - STATE-ASSESSED PROPERTY PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,563] This program   values and assesses   inter-county pipelines and properties owned or used by railroads, regulated telephone  

[7:1:66,573] companies, companies transmitting or selling gas or electricity, and private railroad car companies. Local jurisdictions use the  

[7:2:66,584] established values for the levy and collection of local property taxes. In addition, the BOE collects the Private Railroad Car Tax  

[7:3:66,594] that is deposited in the state General Fund.  

[7:4:66,611] 0570150 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE TAX PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,632] This program collects the excise tax imposed on the sale, distribution, or importation of alcoholic beverages in California. The  

[8:1:66,642] BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer this program.  

[8:2:66,660] 0570575 - INSURANCE TAX PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,680] This program provides revenue to the Insurance Tax Fund. Revenue is generated from taxes assessed on insurance  

[9:1:66,690] premiums, underwriting profits from ocean marine insurance, and retaliatory assessments levied on   out-of-state insurers. The  

[9:2:66,701] taxes collected are used to pay refunds or transferred to the General Fund. The BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer  

[9:3:66,711] this program.  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[8:0:226,380] 0870   Office of Tax Appeals  

[8:1:66,402] The Office of Tax Appeals (OTA) was established effective January 1, 2018, by Chapter 16, Statutes of 2017 (AB 102). The  

[8:2:66,412] OTA performs those tax appeal duties formerly assigned by statute to the State Board of Equalization, including personal  

[8:3:66,422] income tax appeals, franchise tax appeals, and sales and use tax appeals. The OTA's mission is to ensure tax appeals are  

[8:4:66,432] performed in a fair, transparent, consistent, equitable, and impartial manner.  

[9:0:66,453] The OTA has hearing offices in Sacramento, Fresno, and Los Angeles.

[6:0:236,355] 0890   Secretary of State  

[7:0:66,377] The Secretary of State, a constitutionally established office, is the chief elections officer of the state and is responsible for the  

[7:1:66,387] administration and enforcement of election laws. The Office also is responsible for administering and enforcing laws pertaining  

[7:2:66,397] to filing documents associated with corporations, limited liability companies, partnerships, limited partnerships, unincorporated  

[7:3:66,407] associations and pertaining to filing bonds and perfecting security agreements. In addition, the Office is responsible for  

[7:4:66,418] commissioning notaries public, enforcing the notary laws, and in conjunction with being the home of the State Archives,  

[8:0:66,428] administering a state records management program and preserving documents and records having historical significance. The  

[8:1:66,438] Secretary of State is the filing officer for lobbying and campaign registration and disclosure documents filed under the Political  

[8:2:66,448] Reform Act. The Secretary of State also operates the Safe at Home program, maintains the Domestic Partners and Advance  

[8:3:66,458] Health Care Directives registries, provides support functions for the Voting Modernization Board, and is home to the California  

[8:4:66,469] Museum.  

[9:0:66,489] Policy associated with the administration of the Office is accomplished through the divisions of Elections, Political Reform,  

[9:1:66,499] Business Programs, Archives, Information Technology, and Management Services.

[3:0:66,69] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[4:0:65,88] • Fee Relief for New Businesses—The Budget includes $39.8 million one-time General Fund to waive first-time filing fees for  

[4:1:76,98] new businesses registering with the Secretary of State from July 1, 2022 through June 30, 2023.  

[5:0:65,115] • Augmentation of Rent Funding—The Budget includes $3.6 million ($1.7 million General Fund and $1.9 million Business Fees  

[5:1:76,125] Fund) in 2022-23, and $4 million annual thereafter, to support increased rental costs for the Secretary of State headquarters  

[5:2:76,135] building in Sacramento.  

[6:0:65,151] • Expanding Space and Resources for California’s Historic Artifacts and Records—The Budget includes $1 million General  

[6:1:76,161] Fund in 2022-23, and $646,000 annually thereafter, to convert existing storage space and expand protective measures for  

[6:2:76,172] historic records housed in the State Archives.  

[7:0:65,188] • Secretary of State Security Improvements—The Budget includes $2.7 million one-time ($808,000 General Fund and $1.9  

[7:1:76,198] million Business Fees Fund) for the completion of a multi-phased security improvement project, at the March Fong Eu  

[7:2:76,208] Secretary of State Building Complex.  

[8:0:65,224] • Secretary of State Fiscal Staffing Needs—The Budget includes $951,000 ($664,000 Business Fees Fund and $287,000  

[8:1:76,235] General Fund) in 2022-23 and $916,000 annually thereafter to position the Secretary of State with the resources necessary  

[8:2:76,245] to perform the agency’s budget functions effectively and successfully.  

[9:0:65,261] • Elections: Voter Hotline Staffing—The Budget includes $540,000 ongoing General Fund for the use of temporary staff to  

[9:1:76,271] assist with statewide election voter support on the Secretary of State’s Voter Hotline.  

[10:0:65,287] • Voter's Choice Act Resources—The Budget includes $452,000 General Fund in 2022-23 and $437,000 annually thereafter  

[10:1:76,298] for the continued administration of the Voter’s Choice Act of 2016 mandates.  

[11:0:65,314] • Help America Vote Act—The Budget includes $13.9 million one-time Federal Trust Fund to continue implementation of  

[11:1:76,324] statewide mandates of the Help America Vote Act of 2002 ($3.7 million) and pay for costs associated with the VoteCal  

[11:2:76,334] statewide voter registration system ($10.2 million).  

[12:0:65,350] • Improvements to the Project Management Office Structure—The Budget includes ongoing funding of $1.3 million ($398,000  

[12:1:76,361] General Fund and $949,000 Business Fees Fund) to right-size the Project Management Office and Project Portfolio Unit.  

[13:0:65,377] • CAL-ACCESS Replacement System Project—The Budget includes $1 million one-time ($500,000 General Fund and  

[13:1:76,387] $500,000 Political Disclosure, Accountability, Transparency, and Access Fund) to support the costs for the Cal-Access  

[13:2:76,397] Replacement System project restart including pre-planning and planning activities. In addition, provisional language is  

[13:3:76,407] included in the Budget to direct the operation of the funds.  

[14:0:65,424] • California Business Connect Project—The Budget includes $8.1 million one-time funding ($6.6 million Business Fees Fund  

[14:1:76,434] and $1.5 million Business Programs Modernization Fund) to continue implementation of the California Business Connect  

[14:2:76,444] project.  

[15:0:65,460] • Business Programs Division Processing Times—The Budget includes $5.3 million one-time Business Fees Fund to maintain  

[15:1:76,470] manual processing times for statements of information and business entity filings until the full implementation of California  

[15:2:76,481] Business Connect.  

[16:0:65,497] • Campaign Disclosure: Limited Liability Companies (Chapter 321, Statutes of 2021 (SB 686))—The Budget includes  

[16:1:76,507] $566,000 General Fund in 2022-23, and $125,000 annually thereafter, to handle the increased filing activity and assistance  

[16:2:76,517] needed as a result of SB 686.  

[17:0:65,533] • California New Motor Voter Program Task Force (Chapter 314, Statutes of 2021 (AB 796))—The Budget includes $481,000  

[17:1:76,544] General Fund in 2022-23, and $466,000 annually thereafter, to support the task force required by AB 796.

[6:0:66,534] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,553] 0700 - FILINGS AND REGISTRATIONS  

[7:0:66,574] The Business Programs Division is comprised of three primary areas: Business Entities, Uniform Commercial Code, and  

[7:1:66,584] Notary Public and Special Filings.  

[8:0:66,604] Business Entities examines, files, and maintains formation documents for new California business entities and qualifies out-of-

[8:1:66,615] state and international entities to conduct business in California; and also examines, files and maintains changes to the records  

[8:2:66,625] of domestic or qualified foreign business entities to ensure the business entities are properly formed, merged, converted,  

[8:3:66,635] amended, and dissolved in compliance with California law. Statements of Information containing key officers and contact  

[8:4:66,645] information are also processed and maintained for public and governmental use.  

[9:0:66,666] Uniform Commercial Code files certain financing statements allowing lending institutions to protect their financial interest in  

[9:1:66,676] personal property and established priority in case of debtor default or bankruptcy. Notices of judgment liens, attachment liens,  

[9:2:66,686] agricultural liens, and equipment liens are also filed in Uniform Commercial Code, as well as notices of various tax liens  

[9:3:66,696] submitted by state and federal taxing agencies such as the Franchise Tax Board and the Internal Revenue Service.  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 212 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — LJE   210 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:201,32] 0890   Secretary of State - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] Notary Public and Special Filings appoints and commissions qualified notaries public for four- year terms, reviews and  

[4:0:66,79] approves notary public education courses, and certifies to the authenticity of signatures of notaries public and public officials on  

[4:1:66,89] documents for use in foreign countries. Special Filings include trademarks and service marks as well as surety bonds that  

[4:2:66,99] certain business entities are required to file, notices of joint power agreements, city and county charters, and claims for  

[4:3:66,109] successor-in-interest. This area also has disciplinary functions with regard to notaries public and immigration consultants.  

[5:0:66,130] The Advance Health Care Directive (AHCD) Registry maintains AHCDs, which allow a person to indicate his/her medical  

[5:1:66,140] treatment preferences if he/she cannot speak or make decisions for him/herself. The AHCD also may designate someone else  

[5:2:66,150] to make decisions regarding medical treatment. AHCDs and related information can be provided upon request to the  

[5:3:66,160] registrant's health care provider, public guardian, or legal representative.  

[6:0:66,181] The Domestic Partners Registry registers same-sex couples regardless of the age of the partners, and opposite-sex couples in  

[6:1:66,191] which one partner is at least 62 years old, as domestic partners in California.  

[7:0:66,211] The Victims of Corporate Fraud Compensation Fund provides limited restitution to victims of corporate fraud who are unable to  

[7:1:66,222] collect through other means on a judgment against a corporation for corporate fraud.  

[8:0:66,239] Safe at Home is a confidential mail forwarding program designed to assist victims and survivors of domestic violence and  

[8:1:66,250] human trafficking, sexual assault, stalking, elder/dependent adult abuse, their household members and minor children, and  

[8:2:66,260] reproductive healthcare employees, patients, and volunteers. Participants in the Safe at Home program are provided with a  

[8:3:66,270] free post office box to use as a substitute mailing address, thereby reducing or eliminating the need to use their actual  

[8:4:66,280] residential address. Once enrolled into the program, Safe at Home serves as a liaison for those participants who qualify for  

[8:5:66,290] additional confidential services offered by various state and local agencies.  

[9:0:66,308] 0705 - ELECTIONS  

[10:0:66,328] The Secretary of State serves as California’s chief elections officer and has broad responsibility to administer and oversee  

[10:1:66,339] federal and state elections held within California. The Elections Program maintains the official statewide database of registered  

[10:2:66,349] voters, tracks and certifies ballot measures, certifies candidates for placement on the ballot, and certifies official election  

[10:3:66,359] results. In addition, the program oversees the certification and modernization of voting equipment and the enhancement of  

[10:4:66,369] election processes. The program works to increase accessibility to voters, provides resources to educate voters on the  

[10:5:66,379] electoral system, and investigates election related criminal violations as provided by the California Elections Code.  

[11:0:66,400] This program includes the campaign and lobbying registration and disclosure provisions of the Political Reform Act of 1974.  

[11:1:66,410] Under this law, the Office registers all levels of campaign committees, and reviews for compliance with statutory requirements  

[11:2:66,420] all state-level candidate and campaign recipient committees, major donors, slate mailer, political party, and independent  

[11:3:66,430] expenditure committees. The program registers lobbyists (including placement agents), lobbying firms and lobbyist employers,  

[11:4:66,441] reviews for compliance with statutory requirements the periodic financial disclosure reports filed by lobbying entities, and  

[11:5:66,451] publishes a Lobbying Directory on the Internet. This program also supports the electronic filing requirements of the Political  

[11:6:66,461] Reform Act and posts relevant registration and disclosure information to the Office's web site so the public can track where  

[11:7:66,471] campaign money is raised and spent and what lobbying activity is occurring in state government. A searchable database of  

[11:8:66,481] campaign and lobbying financial activity is also provided through the web site.  

[12:0:66,499] 0710 - ARCHIVES  

[13:0:66,517] The California State Archives establishes and administers a records management program that applies efficient and  

[13:1:66,527] economical management methods to the creation, utilization, maintenance, retention, preservation, and disposal of state  

[13:2:66,537] records and acquires, indexes, preserves, and provides reference access to irreplaceable historic materials from the three  

[13:3:66,547] branches of state government. The Archives acquires physical and electronic records with legal, administrative or evidentiary  

[13:4:66,558] value, or that have historical significance. Materials are transferred to the Archives for permanent preservation.  

[14:0:66,575] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[15:0:66,596] This program develops and manages overall policy. It serves as the liaison to other state agencies, the Legislature, the federal  

[15:1:66,606] government, and other states' Secretaries of State. This program responds to constituent correspondence and requests from  

[15:2:66,616] the public and advocates in the Legislature, administers the Secretary's role as a member of the National Association of  

[15:3:66,626] Secretaries of State, in the management of task forces and advisory committees, in the implementation of new federal and  

[15:4:66,637] state statutory requirements, and coordinates and disseminates information about the Office and its initiatives to the public.  

[15:5:66,647] This program also monitors elections cybersecurity incidents and promotes transparency in alerting the public regarding false  

[15:6:66,657] election websites and information as well as providing oversight on cybersecurity risk management.   It also provides the Office  

[15:7:66,667] with the necessary personnel, general administrative, budgeting, fiscal services, and information technology expertise to plan,  

[15:8:66,677] develop, implement, and operate innovative and effective business and information systems solutions.  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[6:0:66,437] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,456] 0740010 - INVESTMENT SERVICES  

[7:0:66,477] The Investment Division is responsible for investment of state monies from the date of receipt through the date of redemption.  

[7:1:66,487] During the 2020-21 fiscal year, this Division handled 11,021 security investment transactions totaling $524.9 billion. The Pooled  

[7:2:66,497] Money Investment Board (PMIB) program accounted for 9,721 of these transactions totaling $487.5 billion; time deposits  

[7:3:66,507] accounted for 932 transactions totaling $26.1 billion. The remaining $11.3 billion is invested on behalf of the state's special  

[7:4:66,517] funds, such as those associated with the California Housing Finance Agency, the Department of Fish and Wildlife, the state's  

[7:5:66,528] retirement system, etc. The Division also administers the Local Agency Investment Fund (LAIF), a voluntary investment  

[7:6:66,538] program created to offer California local agencies greater access to the financial markets through the PMIB program. In the  

[7:7:66,548] 2020-21 fiscal year, 2,387 local agencies participated in LAIF, with deposits averaging $34.0 billion for the fiscal year.  

[7:8:66,566] 0740019 - CENTRALIZED TREASURY AND SECURITIES MANAGEMENT  

[8:0:66,583] In 1949, the California Legislature amended Government Code Section 16305 to create the Centralized Treasury System  

[8:1:66,594] (CTS) thereby requiring agencies of the State to deposit their money in trust with the Treasurer. The legislation also requires  

[8:2:66,604] the Treasurer to safeguard the money and make safe and prudent investments. In 1955, the Legislature created the PMIB,  

[8:3:66,614] giving the Board the responsibility to designate the amount of money available for the investment in securities, bank deposits,  

[8:4:66,624] and loans to the General Fund.  

[9:0:66,642] The Centralized Treasury and Securities Management Division (CTSMD) oversees all banking aspects of the CTS. The goal of  

[9:1:66,652] the CTSMD is to maximize the earning of interest consistent with safe and prudent treasury management, and to ensure that  

[9:2:66,662] the depository banks provide the state with proper and adequate security for the deposit of state monies. The Treasurer  

[9:3:66,673] maintains demand bank accounts with eight banks for the purpose of providing necessary statewide depository coverage for  

[9:4:66,683] the remittance of funds collected by the various state agencies.  

[10:0:66,700] The CTSMD 1) monitors the cash flow of all state funds, forecasts cash balances, revenue, expenditures, and the amounts  

[10:1:66,711] available for daily investments, 2) ensures accurate and timely agency deposits, 3) administers and executes the wire transfer  

[11:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:2:66,89] pledged to the state, 6) fulfills the clearance and settlement of securities pledged to the state for the time, demand, and other  

[3:3:66,99] state agency programs, and 7) is responsible for the safekeeping of securities and other personal property owned by or  

[3:4:66,109] pledged to the state.  

[3:5:66,127] 0740028 - PUBLIC FINANCE  

[4:0:66,148] The Public Finance Division is responsible for selling State of California general obligation bonds, commercial paper notes,  

[4:1:66,158] revenue anticipation notes, lease revenue bonds, revenue bonds, and any other indebtedness for all state agencies. The  

[4:2:66,168] Division provides debt administration services for most state bonds and is responsible for disseminating information to  

[4:3:66,178] bondholders through the Investor Relations Program.  

[5:0:66,199] The Division also assures compliance with federal tax laws applicable to certain state debt so there is no adverse  

[5:1:66,209] consequences to bondholders or increased borrowing costs to the state. The post-issuance tax compliance   includes monitoring  

[5:2:66,219] the use of bond proceeds, managing rebate and yield restriction compliance, coordinating necessary financial disclosure, and  

[5:3:66,229] ensuring proper record keeping.  

[6:0:66,247] 0740035 - ADMINISTRATION AND INFORMATION SERVICES  

[7:0:66,265] The Administration Division, Executive Office, and the Information Services Division provide executive direction and support  

[7:1:66,275] services to programs in the State Treasurer's Office. Services include budgeting, personnel, accounting, information systems,  

[7:2:66,285] business services, technical support, and production operations.

[6:0:134,252] 0956   California Debt and Investment Advisory Commission  

[7:0:66,273] The mission of the California Debt and Investment Advisory Commission is to support and improve the practice of public  

[7:1:66,283] finance in California by providing responsive and reliable information, analysis, and training. The Commission assists California  

[7:2:66,293] state and local governments to monitor, issue, and manage public debt and to safely and prudently invest public funds.  

[8:0:66,314] The Commission consists of nine members including the State Treasurer, who serves as chairperson; the Governor or, upon  

[8:1:66,324] his designation, the Director of Finance; the State Controller; two local government finance officers appointed by the State  

[8:2:66,334] Treasurer; two members of the Assembly appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly; and two members of the Senate  

[8:3:66,344] appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules.

[5:0:66,274] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,293] 0800 - CALIFORNIA DEBT AND INVESTMENT ADVISORY COMMISSION  

[6:0:66,314] The Commission's primary objective is to enhance the knowledge of public officials with respect to the administration and  

[6:1:66,324] issuance of public debt and the investment of public funds. The Commission achieves this objective by performing functions in  

[6:2:66,334] three principal areas, including:  

[7:0:65,352] • Data Collection and Analysis - Serves as a clearinghouse of debt issued by California public entities and nonprofit student  

[7:1:76,362] loan corporations.  

[8:0:65,378] • Continuing Education - Provides educational seminars, workshops, and conferences to public officials on municipal debt and  

[8:1:76,389] public fund investment topics. In addition, the Commission provides technical assistance to public officials and taxpayers  

[8:2:76,399] through direct interaction and public forums to disseminate relevant information.  

[8:3:65,415] • Policy Research - Undertakes original research on the issuance and administration of public debt and on the investment of  

[8:4:76,425] public funds. Research results are published in the form of reports, issue briefs, or articles and are disseminated in printed  

[8:5:76,435] and electronic forms.

[13:0:165,610] 0959   California Debt Limit Allocation Committee  

[13:1:66,632] The California Debt Limit Allocation Committee's mission is to allocate tax-exempt, private activity bond authority for the State  

[13:2:66,642] of California. Private activity bonds may be used by the private sector for projects and programs that provide a public benefit,  

[13:3:66,652] such as the creation of affordable housing.  

[14:0:66,670] The federal government limits the total amount of tax-exempt private activity bond authority that can be issued on an annual  

[14:1:66,680] basis. The bond authority limit (debt limit) is calculated by multiplying the state population by $110 in 2021; a factor determined  

[14:2:66,690] by the IRS each year. California's limit totaled over $4.3 billion in 2021.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,88] 0810 - CALIFORNIA DEBT LIMIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE  

[4:0:66,116] The Committee administers various programs that are funded through the allocation and issuance of tax-exempt private activity  

[4:1:66,126] bonds. Below is a summary of each program:  

[5:0:66,144] Qualified Residential Rental Project Program - Tax-exempt housing revenue bonds lower the cost to develop multifamily rental  

[5:1:66,154] housing, to acquire land and construct new housing, or purchase and rehabilitate existing housing. The developers produce  

[5:2:66,164] affordable rental housing for low-income households by reducing rental rates charged to these individuals and families. To  

[5:3:66,175] qualify, developers must elect either to reserve at least 20% of the units for households earning up to 50% AMI or reserve at  

[5:4:66,185] least 40% of the units for households earning up to 60% AMI. Projects that receive an award of bond authority can apply for  

[5:5:66,195] four-percent tax credits using the California Debt Limit Allocation Committee/California Tax Credit Allocation Committee Joint  

[5:6:66,205] Application.  

[6:0:66,223] Exempt Facility Program - Tax-exempt private activity bonds issued to finance any of the following facilities identified by the IRS  

[6:1:66,233] as an exempt facility, including but not limited to: solid waste disposal and waste recycling facilities, mass commuting facilities,  

[6:2:66,243] high-speed rail, energy and power generating facilities, and sustainable design facilities. Loan interest rate savings enable the  

[6:3:66,253] project owners to charge lower customer rates, while assisting communities they serve to meet mandated requirements to  

[6:4:66,264] protect and enhance the environment.  

[7:0:66,281] Single-Family Housing Program - Tax-exempt mortgage revenue bonds or mortgage credit certificates to assist first-time  

[7:1:66,292] homebuyers with purchasing homes. Homebuyers may purchase single-family homes, either freestanding or detached,  

[7:2:66,302] condominiums, or townhouses. Program participants must meet income limits and must purchase a home that falls within the  

[7:3:66,312] program's purchase price limitations.  

[8:0:66,330] Industrial Development Bond Project Program - Small-Issue industrial development bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds  

[8:1:66,340] issued to assist manufacturing facilities finance capital expenditures. These bonds offer interest rate savings to small and  

[8:2:66,350] midsize manufacturers in contrast to conventional loans, and help manufacturers retain and create new jobs within their  

[8:3:66,360] communities.  

[9:0:66,418] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM  

[10:0:393,440] 2020-21* 2021-22* 2022-23*

[6:2:66,331] construction of new capacity or improvements for the state transportation system in a manner that will help achieve the state's  

[6:3:66,341] goals of reducing greenhouse gas, improving air quality, and conserving natural resources.  

[7:0:66,362] The Authority consists of seven members: the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the Director of the Department of Finance, the  

[7:1:66,372] State Controller, the Director of Transportation, the Executive Director of the California Transportation Commission, a local  

[7:2:66,382] agency representative appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules, and a local agency representative appointed by the  

[7:3:66,392] Speaker of the Assembly.

[4:0:166,116] 0968   California Tax Credit Allocation Committee  

[5:0:66,138] The mission of the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee is to fairly allocate federal and state tax credits to create and  

[5:1:66,148] maintain safe, quality affordable rental housing for low-income households in California.  

[6:0:66,166] The Committee assists development of rental housing projects for low-income families and monitors these projects for years  

[6:1:66,176] after they are placed in service to ensure compliance with federal and state tax credit program requirements of the Internal  

[6:2:66,186] Revenue Service, State law and the Committee. Coordinating with state and local housing fund providers, and with private  

[6:3:66,196] investors, the Committee helps to create and maintain a supply of quality, affordable housing throughout California.  

[6:4:66,214] The Committee consists of seven members, including five voting members and two advisors. The voting members are the  

[6:5:66,224] Treasurer (Chairperson of the Committee), the Governor (who may choose the Director of Finance as his or her  

[7:0:66,234] representative), the State Controller, the Director of Housing and Community Development, and the Executive Director of the  

[7:1:66,244] California Housing Finance Agency. The non-voting (advisory) members are two local government representatives. One local  

[7:2:66,255] representative is associated with a city government and appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly. The other is a county  

[7:3:66,265] government representative appointed by the Senate Rules Committee.

[5:0:66,365] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,384] 0840 - CALIFORNIA TAX CREDIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE  

[7:0:66,405] The Federal Program  

[8:0:66,422] Congress authorized the federal Low-Income Housing Tax Credit (LIHTC) program in 1986. It replaced traditional housing tax  

[8:1:66,432] incentives, such as accelerated depreciation, with a tax credit that enables developers of affordable rental housing to raise  

[8:2:66,443] project equity through the "sale" of tax benefits to investors. The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling is calculated annually and  

[8:3:66,453] indexed for inflation.  

[9:0:66,471] Two types of federal tax credits are available, generally referred to as 9-percent and 4-percent credits. These terms refer to the  

[9:1:66,481] percentage of a project's "qualified basis" an investor in LIHTC projects may deduct from his or her federal income tax liability  

[9:2:66,491] annually in each of ten years. A project's qualified basis is the portion of the total project cost used to calculate the amount of  

[9:3:66,501] the tax credit and typically excludes non-depreciable costs such as the purchase of land. The affordable housing project  

[9:4:66,511] sponsor uses or sells ten times the project's tax-credit allocation amount because investors can take the annual tax credit each  

[9:5:66,522] year for a ten-year period.  

[10:0:66,539] The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling for 9-percent credits is calculated annually and indexed for inflation. For 2021, each  

[10:1:66,549] state has an annual housing credit ceiling of $2.81 per state resident. Additionally, each state may qualify annually for a share  

[10:2:66,560] of unused credits in a national pool.  

[11:0:66,577] Developments financed with tax-exempt bond proceeds may receive the 4% federal tax credit. The sponsors of such projects  

[11:1:66,588] must apply to the Committee and must conform to applicable federal and state statutory and regulatory requirements, but there  

[11:2:66,598] is no annual cap on the amount of credit that may be awarded by the state to such developments.  

[11:3:66,615] Under federal law, credit projects must remain affordable for at least 30 years. However, California's program generally requires  

[11:4:66,626] maintaining affordability for 55 years. Land use agreements are recorded against each credit project to ensure compliance.  

[11:5:66,643] The State LIHTC Program  

[12:0:66,661] In 1987, recognizing the high cost of housing in California, the Legislature authorized the state's program to augment the  

[12:1:66,671] federal program. Housing projects receiving (or that have previously received) an allocation of federal tax credits may apply for  

[12:2:66,681] an allocation of state tax credits. Projects serving farmworkers may apply for state tax credits regardless of their federal tax  

[12:3:66,692] credit status.  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:410,13] 2022-23 STATE BUDGET — LJE   241 

[2:0:131,32] 0968   California Tax Credit Allocation Committee - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The annual state credit ceiling is indexed for inflation, and for 2021, was $109.7 million. Investors take the state tax credit  

[3:1:66,79] annually over a four-year period in contrast to the ten-year federal period.  

[3:2:66,97] Chapter 159, Statutes of 2019, authorized the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee and the California Debt Limit  

[3:3:66,107] Allocation Committee to issue an additional $500 million in state tax credits in 2020 to be paired with the 4% federal program to  

[3:4:66,117] bolster new construction of low income housing. Per AB 83, this $500 million tax credit was issued in 2021 pursuant to an  

[3:5:66,127] authorization in the annual Budget Act or related legislation.  

[3:6:66,145] Farmworker Housing Program  

[4:0:66,163] Chapter 521, Statutes of 2008, folded the previous Farmworker Housing Assistance Tax Credit program into the general state  

[4:1:66,173] LIHTC program as a $500,000 annual set-aside in support of farmworker housing. Pursuant to Chapter 372, Statutes of 2017,  

[4:2:66,183] these credits differ from other state credits in that the credit percentage for tax-exempt bond financed projects is higher and  

[4:3:66,193] projects may receive state credits even if they receive a federal tax credit basis increase.

[4:0:88,180] 0971   California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing  

[4:1:279,195] Authority  

[4:2:66,216] The California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing Authority was established by Chapter 908, Statutes  

[4:3:66,226] of 1980, to promote the prompt and efficient development of energy sources which are renewable or which more efficiently  

[4:4:66,237] utilize and conserve scarce energy resources. Recognizing the importance of developing a secure energy future to protect the  

[4:5:66,247] environment and ensure economic stability, the Authority advances the state's goals of reducing greenhouse gas emissions by  

[4:6:66,257] providing financing options to assist industries in increasing the deployment of sustainable and renewable energy sources,  

[4:7:66,267] implementing measures that increase the efficiency of the use of energy, creating high quality employment opportunities, and  

[4:8:66,277] lessening the state's dependence on fossil fuels. To support these goals, the Authority provides financing and credit  

[4:9:66,288] enhancements to promote the establishment of facilities that use alternative methods and sources of energy, and facilities  

[4:10:66,298] needed for the development and commercialization of advanced transportation technologies.  

[5:0:66,318] The Authority consists of five members: the State Treasurer, who serves as the chairperson, the State Controller, the Director  

[5:1:66,328] of the Department of Finance, the Chairperson of the State Energy Resources Conservation and Development Commission,  

[5:2:66,339] and the President of the Public Utilities Commission.

[6:0:66,396] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:0:66,415] 0850 - ALTERNATIVE ENERGY AND ADVANCED TRANSPORTATION FINANCING AUTHORITY  

[8:0:66,436] Financial assistance can take the form of loans, loan loss reserves, interest rate reductions, proceeds of bonds issued by the  

[8:1:66,446] Authority,   loan guarantees or other credit enhancements, contributions of money, or a combination thereof, as determined and  

[8:2:66,456] approved by resolution of the Authority.  

[9:0:66,474] The Authority is a conduit issuer of tax-exempt private activity bonds to finance local district heating or cooling facilities, and  

[9:1:66,484] private activity bonds for 501(c)(3) non-profits. Past issuances total more than $212 million in bond financing for green projects  

[9:2:66,494] in California.  

[10:0:66,515] In 2010, the Authority launched a sales and use tax exclusion (STE) program for advanced transportation and alternative  

[10:1:66,525] source manufacturing in California (Chapter 10, Statutes of 2010). The STE program   expanded   (Chapter 677, Statutes of  

[10:2:66,535] 2012)   to include advanced manufacturing, with an annual cap of $100 million available for STE awards. Chapter 768, Statutes  

[10:3:66,545] of 2015, further expanded the program to also include equipment primarily used to process recycled feedstock and equipment  

[10:4:66,555] that primarily utilizes recycled feedstock in the production of another product.   In 2019, Chapter 690, Statutes of 2019, extended  

[10:5:66,566] the STE program sunset date to January 1, 2026, and Chapter 672, Statutes of 2019, expanded the job creation-related criteria  

[10:6:66,576] by which CAEATFA must evaluate applications. The objective of this program is to promote the creation of California-based  

[10:7:66,586] manufacturing, businesses, and jobs that are aimed at reducing greenhouse gases, air and water pollution, and energy  

[10:8:66,596] consumption.  

[11:0:66,617] Legislation in 2010 (Chapter 15, Statutes of 2010), 2011 (Chapter 9, Statutes of 2011, First Extraordinary Session), and 2013  

[11:1:66,627] (Chapter 356, Statutes of 2013), authorized financial assistance to encourage energy efficiency retrofits. The Authority  

[11:2:66,637] developed a loan loss reserve program   for residential whole house energy efficiency and renewable energy projects, and   a risk  

[11:3:66,647] mitigation program for residential Property Assessed Clean Energy programs in California. Programs to support low-interest  

[11:4:66,657] financing of Property Assessed Clean Energy efficiency projects in commercial buildings are in discussion.  

[12:0:66,678] The Budget Act of 2014 authorized administration of the California Hub for Energy Efficiency Financing on behalf of, and in  

[12:1:66,688] collaboration with, the California Public Utilities Commission   to develop and launch energy efficiency financing pilot programs   to  

[12:2:66,698] encourage and leverage private capital lending   (in both the residential and commercial sectors). These programs   employ  

[12:3:66,708] various types of credit enhancements, lower costs and expand access to capital for Californians making   energy efficiency  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[11:0:151,573] 0974   California Pollution Control Financing Authority  

[12:0:66,594] California Pollution Control Financing Authority (CPCFA) is committed to stimulating local economies in California by making  

[12:1:66,604] capital more accessible to small businesses and delivering innovative financing for projects that protect and restore the  

[12:2:66,615] environment.  

[13:0:66,632] Created in 1972, CPCFA originated as a conduit issuer of tax-exempt, pollution-control bonds and now assists the solid-waste,  

[13:1:66,642] recycling, water, and wastewater industries through its Private Activity Tax-Exempt Bond Program. Over the last 50 years,  

[13:2:66,653] CPCFA evolved to include financing programs assisting California's small business sector through its California Capital Access  

[13:3:66,663] Program (CalCAP) and to promote the reuse and redevelopment of brownfields through the California Recycle Underutilized  

[13:4:66,673] Sites Program (CALReUSE).  

[14:0:66,693] CPCFA consists of the following members: State Treasurer (Chairperson), the State Controller, and the Director of the  

[14:1:66,704] Department of Finance.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE
